<div id="review_181190446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181190446" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181190446?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      Maja, Flannery, Jo
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181190446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14037098422122948583">This is a very successful and fully realized first person point of view. Jeff’s feelings and experiences are enveloping. In some ways I feel like the major themes in this book need to be spoiled, because it will attract more readers. But on the other hand, I think that it was a real stroke of genius for the author to leave us in the dark. Jeff would rather forget and reject himself, and so by extension, do we. We only come to realize what Jeff is going through in small degrees, which perfectly m</span>
  <span id="freeText14037098422122948583" style="display:none">This is a very successful and fully realized first person point of view. Jeff’s feelings and experiences are enveloping. In some ways I feel like the major themes in this book need to be spoiled, because it will attract more readers. But on the other hand, I think that it was a real stroke of genius for the author to leave us in the dark. Jeff would rather forget and reject himself, and so by extension, do we. We only come to realize what Jeff is going through in small degrees, which perfectly mirrors the uncertainty and shame that he experiences.<br /><br />When Jeff wakes up in the psych ward of the hospital and is told that he’ll be staying there for forty five days of treatment, he’s outraged. There’s absolutely nothing wrong with him. He doesn’t need to answer the stupid questionnaires or do role plays with the other, obviously crazier, patients. The bandages on his wrists are nothing, just a bit of juvenile melodrama. Everyone tries it once, right?<br /><br />Jeff hides behind a thick layer of sarcasm and anger, which brings a surprising amount of lightness and humor to this book. His late night movie narrations with Sadie, his “therapy” sessions with Dr. <s>Cat Poop</s> Katzrupus, and his rapport with his sister Amanda all had me snickering. But there is also a strong undercurrent of dread, as Jeff’s anxiety about his life outside the hospital and his fear of a part of himself that can’t be ignored begin to grow. When Jeff finally lets himself remember the circumstances leading up to his suicide, I was so consumed by his feelings that I found myself cringing with shame and embarrassment. I had to retreat back into my own head, where I could see everything more clearly. <br /><br />I love that neither Jeff nor any of the other patients are magically cured. Maybe they’ll get better and maybe they won’t. Maybe they can’t. Nothing here is stable, especially not identity. Identity can’t be declared or set in stone; it’s ever-changing. And I like how he presents another side of this coin in Rankin, who so completely hates and rejects himself that he’s incapable of seeing anything clearly. I felt so sad for Rankin, but the next minute I wanted to give him my frostiest mom glare and tell him to <i>leave my boy alone.</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I felt so much pain for Jeff. How I wished that he could have the awkward dates, the first kisses, the anniversaries and school dances, instead of accepting this attention from Rankin. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Bright Eyes – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bjHACWmO0jQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Poison Oak</a><br /><br />Well, this song is very much a spoiler for some of the major themes in this book…so here’s my underhanded way of revealing a few plot points without actually putting them in my review. Mwa ha ha! The lyrics are sad, angry, and wistful as he remembers someone who was a close childhood friend and who he lost to suicide.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14037098422122948583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_151296917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151296917" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151296917?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23710603-suicide-notes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2015">reviewed-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-for-rainy-days">books-for-rainy-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151296917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6492346617879497744"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>After an attempted suicide, Jeff wakes up in a psychiatric ward where he is forced to spend the next 45 days. He doesn’t want to and he’s determined not to cooperate, but his stay isn’t optional and his parents refuse to take him home. Finding their son almost bloodless in a bathtub isn’t something they particularly want to relive, and if the psych ward is what it takes to keep him alive, that’s where he’ll stay for as long as it takes. <br/><br/>Jeff handles his situation with lots of denial wra</span>
  <span id="freeText6492346617879497744" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br>After an attempted suicide, Jeff wakes up in a psychiatric ward where he is forced to spend the next 45 days. He doesn’t want to and he’s determined not to cooperate, but his stay isn’t optional and his parents refuse to take him home. Finding their son almost bloodless in a bathtub isn’t something they particularly want to relive, and if the psych ward is what it takes to keep him alive, that’s where he’ll stay for as long as it takes. <br><br>Jeff handles his situation with lots of denial wrapped in good humor. He absolutely refuses to acknowledge that he has a problem and he is determined not to talk about his reasons for cutting his wrists open. According to him, his parents and the doctor made a mistake and he shouldn’t be locked up with the crazies. <br><br>Jeff’s story is heartwarming and poignant, but it’s also simple and laugh-out-loud funny. This diary-like narrative is one of the most honest things I’ve ever read. There are no heroes, no villains, no Big Drama whatsoever. It’s just a story about a boy that could easily be your next door neighbor or your second cousin. It’s not unusual at all and that’s what makes it so special.<br><br>Jeff’s character was truly done brilliantly. He is easily relatable, even (or especially) when he’s being obnoxious to his doctors and his fellow patience. Avoidance is his way to handle everything, but every now and again, a real feeling shines trough, be it anger at his parents for daring to save his life, resentment towards his doctors and nurses and the complete and utter hopelessness he feels about his situation.<br><br>I want to make this very clear: Suicide Notes is a book that deals with serious issues, but it’s rarely a sad read and it’s never angsty. Jeff’s sarcastic voice determines the overall tone, which is more funny than anything else. Yet Ford still manages to bring his point across by making every one of Jeff’s jokes louder and more touching than any sorrowful moment could possibly be.<br><br>I’ve tried this in both formats and while I generally prefer audio, in this case I’d strongly recommend the printed word. Although he’s a good narrator, Joe Caron didn’t succeed in capturing Jeff’s unique voice and most of Jeff’s sarcastic remarks somehow fell flat in the narrator’s interpretation. <br><br>If I had my way (but really, I never do), every thirteen-year-old on the planet would have to read three books: Brooklyn, Burning by Steve Brezenoff, Gone, Gone, Gone by Hannah Moskowitz and Suicide Notes by Michael Thomas Ford. These three books promote understanding and tolerance in such a quiet, unobtrusive way, and even though we’re seeing more and more diversity, these are the three that always stay with me. <br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6492346617879497744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280551597?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/7477266-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062043078" href="/book/show/9952477-suicide-notes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=z2015">z2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280551597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15629358530381701128">This was kind of an average read for me. I didn't think it was really deep or hilarious. There were a few things that Jeff said that made me laugh but I didn't actually like him until like 2/3's of the way in. He became bearable then (and also said some insightful things - listed below). He was snarky and mean and I wasn't impressed at all. I always have an issue with unreliable narrators like Jeff. I mean he doesn't tell us the whole story straight away and I don't understand why not.<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoi</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15629358530381701128" style="display:none">This was kind of an average read for me. I didn't think it was really deep or hilarious. There were a few things that Jeff said that made me laugh but I didn't actually like him until like 2/3's of the way in. He became bearable then (and also said some insightful things - listed below). He was snarky and mean and I wasn't impressed at all. I always have an issue with unreliable narrators like Jeff. I mean he doesn't tell us the whole story straight away and I don't understand why not.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sure, he comes to terms with his sexuality and understanding that it is a part of him but why didn't he tell us the real reason why he tried to kill himself? Maybe he was coming to terms with that too, but he just said he did it because he was 'bored'. Of course, I didn't actually buy that but  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I just don't like narrators who only tell us half the story and kind of leave it until the book is nearly over for some shock factor. <br /><br />The writing was simple but I thought it was effective. It did sound like a 15 year old boy. The other characters were kind of one-dimensional but this is a story about Jeff though so I can understand why. I would have loved to have learned more about the other patients and learned what happened with them after Jeff left but I think we weren't given closure because Jeff probably didn't speak to any of the other patients after he got out. I wasn't really attached to Jeff though so I didn't really care about getting closure with him. <br /><br />It was a quick, short read so I probably would recommend it to those who think it sounds interesting and I would probably read something else by Michael Thomas Ford.<br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br />"I tried to go back to sleep, but my mind was racing, racing, racing. Only I wasn't really thinking about anything specific. It was just this stream of words and half thoughts, like there were a thousand different channels in my brain and someone was flipping through them one after the next."<br /><br />"And just because your life isn't as awful as someone else's, that doesn't mean it doesn't suck. You can't compare how you feel to the way other people feel."<br /><br />"I swear, sometimes it feels like there's this monkey in my head who runs around turning the dials and changing channels on me."<br /><br />"No one ever tells you that when your heart breaks, you can feel it. But you can. It feels like something has crumbled inside you and the pieces are falling into you stomach."<br /><br />"When people hurt us, the best thing to do isn't to ask why they did it but to remind ourselves that it wasn't our fault."<br /></span>

<div id="review_182733320" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182733320" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182733320?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo by: </span>
      MaWen
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182733320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7488683905090568773">4.5 stars.<br/><br/><i>“It’s a really crappy feeling to realize that your entire outlook on your life can be controlled by some little pill that looks like a Pez, and that some weird combination of drugs can make your brain think it’s on a holiday somewhere really sweet when actually you’re standing naked in the middle of the school cafeteria while everyone is takes pictures of you. Metaphorically. Or whatever.”</i><br/><br/><b>High Points.</b><br/>I actually choked with laughter on my panad at approximately 90% of this book. The oth</span>
  <span id="freeText7488683905090568773" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br /><i>“It’s a really crappy feeling to realize that your entire outlook on your life can be controlled by some little pill that looks like a Pez, and that some weird combination of drugs can make your brain think it’s on a holiday somewhere really sweet when actually you’re standing naked in the middle of the school cafeteria while everyone is takes pictures of you. Metaphorically. Or whatever.”</i><br /><br /><b>High Points.</b><br />I actually choked with laughter on my panad at approximately 90% of this book. The other 10% I was trying to piece my heart back together as it was shattered into smithereens. This book caused very strong reactions in me, as you can probably tell. Friendship. Relationships. Perfect combination of Family. Understanding. Realistic, unflinching portrayal of kids with mental illnesses. Diversity. Siblings. Cat Poop. Watching old films. Acceptance. Hope. Positivity. Gah… I loved this book.<br /><br /><b>Low Points.</b><br />Hmm… this isn’t for the book itself because I honestly can’t think of anything that <i>I</i> didn’t like about it. But I know that this book isn’t for everyone but I’ll cover this in my angst section.<br /><br /><br /><b>Hero.</b><br />OK, I’m just going to put this out there. I love Jeff. Literally, metaphorically and physically, although I don’t think I’d be allowed to break his ‘<i>No Hugging</i>’ rule he has. Sigh. Jeff’s narration is manic, breathless and flits off onto random tangents (<i>“One minute I’m sitting around eating chocolate chip cookies and then all of the sudden I’m thinking about bears.”</i>) but it’s never hard to follow. <br />He is self-deprecating, sarcastic and doesn’t hold anything back…. Except the important things.<br /> What I found the most fascinating/upsetting about Jeff's character was that, yes, he was hilarious and came out with some fantastic one liners… but it often seemed that his humour and deadpan commentary was a knee-jerk reaction. Jeff uses his humour as a defence mechanism and I think that was one of the reasons why, when the going began to get tough and Jeff began to realise that he had to face certain things about himself, I found him so endearing because I could relate and I’m sure a lot of other people could as well. <br />Maybe, at the end of the day, we’re <i>all</i> a bit crazy.<br /><br /><b>Best Friends/Love Interest</b><br />I’m going to go ahead and skip these two because there such an important aspect of, not only the story, but in Jeff’s development and I would hate to spoil it for any people who haven’t read it yet.<br />So just read it so we can discuss!<br /><br /><b>Theme Tune. </b><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4yJkdAZcV5I&amp;feature=related" rel="nofollow noopener">Madness (Is all in the mind)- Madness</a><br /><br /><i>People say that I’m crazy<br />But I’m not that way inclined<br />I know what I know and I’ll happily show<br />That madness is all in the mind.</i><br /><br />A little nod at Jeff and his, shall we say, predicament. I like to think he’d be a Madness fan. <br /><br /><b>Angst Level.</b><br />10/10. I’m going to have to apologise in advance for the vagueness of this section but I don’t want to go into too much detail because I think this book is best read knowing nothing. <br />Like I mentioned earlier, this book isn’t for everyone. There are very graphic descriptions of self-harm and they <i>are</i> shocking and often difficult to read. But Ford perfectly depicts all the raw feelings that Jeff experiences and the scenes are never glorified and he never resorts to sensationalism which some authors tend to when dealing with suicide attempts and self harming. <br />I also loved the way the reader was kept in the dark about the reason behind Jeff’s suicide attempt was cleverly done and highly affective right up until the last few chapters. <br />Even though the angst level is extremely high and this book is harrowing in some points, there is a highly positive vein running through the heart of Jeff’s story. I know not all kids out there going through these issues will get the happy ending that Jeff does, but it’s comforting to know that there is somewhere for them to turn even when there isn’t.<br />I feel like I’m doing this book a huge disservice by dwelling on this side of things because, yes it’s dark… but it’s also one of the most hilarious and heart-warming books I’ve read in a while. <br />I’m really looking forward to reading more from Ford because he it is obvious that he is a talented and capable writer, both with humour but also the serious stuff, too. <br /> <br /><b>Recommended For.</b><br />People who have ever felt there’s no one to turn to. People who love books that are a bit darker than your average. People who give nicknames to people with names they can’t pronounce. People who think they could do a better job at coming up with the dialogue of films. People who always wanted the bigger room that their siblings nabbed. People who feel that The Nutcracker has changed their outlook on life. People who are wondering how you can get to cookies and bears in the same conversation. <br /><br /><br />You can find this review and plenty of other exciting stuff on my blog <a href="http://weartheoldcoat.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7488683905090568773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7307005682372340839" style="display:none">AUGUST 2015 - BOOKTUBEATHON DAY 2:<br /><br /><blockquote> <b> “Just because your life isn’t as awful as someone else’s, that doesn’t mean it doesn’t suck. You can’t compare how you feel to the way other people feel. It just doesn’t work. <i> What might look like the perfect life—or even an okay life—to you might not be so okay for the person living it.” </i> </b> </blockquote><br /><br />This book is so important &amp; powerful. It portrays so many themes and messages so perfectly with such authenticity that Jeff is one of the most uniquely realistic characters I've read.<br /><br />There are so many themes that are dealt with in this book and this makes it a very emotional &amp; thought provoking read.<br /><br />HOWEVER, just because this book may look hella depressing IT IS NOT! It's an hilarious read that had me in fits of laughter in several places -- the humour and sarcasm in this book were top notch!<br /><br />I just love what messages this book conveys and I think everyone will appreciate the importance of honesty with yourself &amp; others around you that this book highlights.<br /><br />One of my favourite books of the year!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9421078405602379572">This was to be a brief, light read between heavier books. Brief, yes. Light, not so much. It was definitely humorous, a 15 year old wakes up in a mental ward after trying to kill himself. Ok, I know that doesn't sound funny, but it's in the delivery. <br/>I knew that part going into it, but around the halfway mark more issues are revealed, to us and the narrator himself. <br/>The journey is short, only 45 days in the ward, but there's certainly a lot going on, involving therapy, parental visits, and other</span>
  <span id="freeText9421078405602379572" style="display:none">This was to be a brief, light read between heavier books. Brief, yes. Light, not so much. It was definitely humorous, a 15 year old wakes up in a mental ward after trying to kill himself. I enjoyed all the supporting characters. <br /><br />Another YA book with adult situations. Recommended.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2677082346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2677082346" />
    <a title="Basyirah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62044561-basyirah"><img alt="Basyirah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552299674p2/62044561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2677082346?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Basyirah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Basyirah" href="/user/show/62044561-basyirah">Basyirah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062043078" href="/book/show/9952477-suicide-notes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677082346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15786474443071365616"><i>And here's what I'm wondering: How come someone always saves the people who try to kill themselves and then makes them tell everyone how sorry they are for ruining their evenings? I keep feeling like everyone wants me to apologize for something. But I'm not going to. I don't have anything to apologize for. They're the ones who screwed everything up. Not me.<br/>I didn't ask to be saved.<br/><br/>- - - -<br/><br/>Am I lucky? Am I lucky that I didn't die? Am I lucky that, compared to the other kids here, my life doesn't s</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15786474443071365616" style="display:none"><i>And here's what I'm wondering: How come someone always saves the people who try to kill themselves and then makes them tell everyone how sorry they are for ruining their evenings? I keep feeling like everyone wants me to apologize for something. But I'm not going to. I don't have anything to apologize for. They're the ones who screwed everything up. Not me.<br />I didn't ask to be saved.<br /><br />- - - -<br /><br />Am I lucky? Am I lucky that I didn't die? Am I lucky that, compared to the other kids here, my life doesn't seem so bad? Maybe I am, but I have to say, I don't feel lucky. For one thing, I'm stuck in this pit. And just because your life isn't as awful as someone else's, that doesn't mean it doesn't suck. You can't compare how you feel to the way other people feel. It just doesn't work. What might look like the perfect life-or even an okay life-to you might not be okay for the person living it.<br /><br />- - - -<br /><br />No one ever tells you that when your heart breaks, you can feel it. But you can. It feels like something has crumbled inside you and the pieces are falling into your stomach. It hurts more than any punch ever could. You stop breathing, and for a while you can't remember how. When you finally do, it feels like your throat has closed up, like you're trying to suck air through a straw.</i><br /><br />- - - -<br /><br />I think books about mental illness or anything at all that closely related to it really appeal to me in a deeper emotional attachment level. Reading Suicide Notes really gave me all kind of feels. Tbh, I might have picked this book up at a wrong time. I'm not feeling so good myself lately. That's why even though it's a rather thin book, it took me a while to finish it. I was stalling because even though it started out as funny and entertaining, I knew itd hurt somehow. I really love how sarcastic and defensive Jeff was. It's his way of coping, even though he didn't know it at the time. Or he refused to acknowledge. His family signed him up for a 45-day therapy thing after his failed attempt to kill himself and he was disappointed, upset and angry. A teenage boy, wanting to escape life, was saved against his own will. I couldn't relate to it on that level but I understand what he was feeling anyway. It's hard not to. This book was about Jeff, so even when the book also discussed about others, but since it's not about them, we don't get specific details about them. However, it's okay not to know. Because maybe then I'd be even more heartbroken. <br /><br />(istg if the author started telling more about Martha and Sadie, it'd depress tf out of me-not Rankin tho, he can go f himself) <br /><br />I was right about this book hurting my feelings. It reminded me of things I didn't want to remember, but it's okay. It burns but it serves as a reminder that scars don't just fade and disappear. I didn't take the book too seriously at first because like I said, Jeff was funny. But then the last ten days before Jeff was allowed to go home, things were getting more intense. And just like that, walls and barriers were broken, as well as my heart. Okay that's probably a spoiler, but well, at least it'd give you the motivation to read it till the end though. .<br /><br />If you're looking for answers and conclusions, then this book is not for you. But what I can tell you is that sometimes, those are not important. But the satisfaction is in the story itself. It doesn't really satisfy me because Jeff's real issues were not discussed earlier in the book, so one month was wasted for nothing. But I guess it opened a wider chance for them all to bond a little more, which made the impact of what happened even bigger and deeper. So would I recommend this slow burn book? I would. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15786474443071365616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1386755990?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea slytherink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea slytherink" href="/user/show/33481873-chelsea-slytherink">Chelsea slytherink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=representation-queer">representation-queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33481873-chelsea-slytherink?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1386755990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3090639478254131902">Actual rating: 3.5 stars [spoiler free review]<br/><br/>Warning: In the book and in this review,mental illness and suicide are mentioned.<br/><br/>The second half of Suicide Notes was much better than the first. A character struggles with (coming to terms with) their sexuality, and I always enjoy reading about that. Nevertheless, I have some issues with the book, mainly with the author's choice of words.<br/><br/>I really liked the following quote: “And just because your life isn’t as awful as someone else’s, that doesn’t me</span>
  <span id="freeText3090639478254131902" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.5 stars [spoiler free review]<br /><br />Warning: In the book and in this review,mental illness and suicide are mentioned.<br /><br />The second half of Suicide Notes was much better than the first. A character struggles with (coming to terms with) their sexuality, and I always enjoy reading about that. Nevertheless, I have some issues with the book, mainly with the author's choice of words.<br /><br />I really liked the following quote: “And just because your life isn’t as awful as someone else’s, that doesn’t mean it doesn’t suck. You can’t compare how you feel to the way other people feel. It just doesn’t work. What might look like the perfect life—or even an okay life—to you might not be so okay for the person living it.”<br /><br />BUT, that's not what the characters thought at all. They made fun of certain mental illnesses, saying they were just doing it for attention: “I thought for sure she’d be into something really girly, like cutting herself.” How in the world is harming yourself girly?! Maybe it's more common with girls than boys, I don't know, but it's clear that she doesn't mean that. And it bothers me even more that a girl says this. I won't even begin to explain what is wrong with the next quote: “Then you’ve got the bulimics and the anorexics. They’re slightly more interesting, although usually they’re just girls with nothing better to do”<br /><br />I didn't like the way the author wrote female characters, just look at the following quote by that female character: “Sure. I’ve made out with lots of my friends. Sometimes more than that.” So this girl says she has kissed (and done even more) with her female friends, just to learn how to do this. I DOUBT GIRLS IN REAL LIFE DO THIS! Seriously, is this some kind of fantasy the author has?! It was so obvious at times that this book was written by a man. I mean, look at this next quote: “I was sort of afraid Juliet, Sadie, and Martha were going to make me play house with them, or have a tea party, or paint our toenails”. Oh yes, of course, because all girls do this.... What an idiot.<br /><br />The main character says "retarded" a couple of times, as in "retarded exercise" for example. English is not my first language and I have known for years that this word is offensive. The author could have gone for stupid, but picked a word with a well known negative connotation instead.<br /><br />My absolute main issue with this book, is the lack of consent! This book contains some sexual scenes, and almost all of them happened while someone was asleep! This is not okay. You can't just crawl into someone's bed and perform sexual acts on them! I do have to say that the characters didn't make the other stop when they woke up, so they were okay with it, but still, it wasn't consent in the first place.<br /><br />Conclusion: Would I recommend this book? Probably not, especially not to people who struggle with their mental health. The character is very insensitive to other people's problems, calls them crazy numerous times because they need help and refuses to admit he is struggling himself. The sexual scenes were very "iffy", there was no consent when it started. I did like the sexuality struggles, because I enjoy reading about that and it was unexpected, but still, this is not the best book out there on mental health.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3090639478254131902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_6609549'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6609549-by-the-time-you-read-this-i-ll-be-dead?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">By the Time You Read This, I&#39;ll Be Dead<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/52989.Julie_Anne_Peters?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Julie Anne Peters<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.87 avg rating &mdash; 21,501 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2009\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer1019868159526247815\">Daelyn Rice is broken beyond repair, and after a string of botched suicide attempts, she’s determined to get her death right. She starts visiting a website for “completers”— www. through-the-light.com.\n\nWhile she’s on the site, Daelyn blogs about her<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1019868159526247815\" style=\"display:none\">Daelyn Rice is broken beyond repair, and after a string of botched suicide attempts, she’s determined to get her death right. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5977920636569758897">Michael Thomas Ford is the author of more than fifty books, for both young readers and adults, in genres ranging from humor to horror, literary fiction to nonfiction. As a writer for young adults he is the author of the popular "Circle of Three" series (writing as Isobel Bird); nonfiction books about spirituality (Paths of Faith), the AIDS crisis (Voices of AIDS), and the gay community (The World </span>
  <span id="freeText5977920636569758897" style="display:none">Michael Thomas Ford is the author of more than fifty books, for both young readers and adults, in genres ranging from humor to horror, literary fiction to nonfiction. As a writer for young adults he is the author of the popular "Circle of Three" series (writing as Isobel Bird); nonfiction books about spirituality (Paths of Faith), the AIDS crisis (Voices of AIDS), and the gay community (The World Out There and Speaking Out); and the novels Suicide Notes and Z (forthcoming in 2010).<br /><br />His work for adult readers includes the best-selling novels Last Summer, Looking for It, Full Circle, Changing Tides, and What We Remember, and Jane Bites Back. His work has been nominated for 12 Lambda Literary Awards, twice winning for Best Humor Book, twice for Best Romance Novel, and most recently for Gay Men's Mystery. He was also nominated for a Horror Writers Association Bram Stoker Award (for his novel The Dollhouse That Time Forgot) and a Gaylactic Spectrum Award (for his short story "Night of the Werepuss"). </span>
